<td align="left" valign="top" width="92%">
<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: arial, sans-serif; FONT-SIZE: 8pt">Royal Bank of Canada is offering Trigger Phoenix Autocallable Notes (the &#8220;Notes&#8221;) linked to the worst performing of two equity indices (each, a &#8220;Reference Index,&#8221; and together, the &#8220;Reference Indices&#8221;). The Notes offered are senior unsecured obligations of Royal Bank of Canada, and will pay a quarterly Continent Coupon at the annual rate of 7.40% if the level of each of the Reference Indices is equal to or greater than its applicable Coupon Barrier.</font></div>
</td>
</tr></table>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: arial, sans-serif; FONT-SIZE: 9pt">If the Notes are automatically called, then, on the applicable Call Settlement Date, for each $1,000 principal amount, you will receive $1,000 plus the Contingent Coupon otherwise due on that Call Settlement Date.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">In <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold">Example 1</font>, the Notes are automatically called following the fourth Observation Date as the closing level of each Reference Index on the fourth Observation Date is greater than its Initial Level.&#160;&#160;Payment will be calculated as follows:</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">Principal Amount + Contingent Coupon = $1,000.00 + $18.50 = $1,018.50</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">In this example, the Call Feature limits the term of your investment to approximately twelve months.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">
<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">
<div style="BORDER-BOTTOM: 0px; TEXT-ALIGN: left; BORDER-LEFT: 0px; PADDING-BOTTOM: 0px; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; PADDING-LEFT: 0px; PADDING-RIGHT: 0px; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; BORDER-TOP: 0px; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; BORDER-RIGHT: 0px; PADDING-TOP: 0px">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">In <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold">Example 2</font>, the Notes are automatically called following the fifth Observation Date, as the closing level of each Reference Index on the fifth Observation Date is greater than its Initial Level.&#160;&#160;(The Notes were not called on the second Observation Date, as the Notes cannot be called until on or after the fourth Observation Date. The Notes were not called on the fourth Observation Date, as the closing level of only one of the Reference Indices was greater than its Initial Level.) As the closing level of each Reference Index on the first four Observation Dates is greater than the Coupon Barrier and Trigger Level, you receive the Contingent Coupon of $18.50 with respect to each of those Observation Dates, for a total of $74.00 in Contingent Coupon payments prior to the automatic call.&#160;&#160;Following the fifth Observation Date, you receive a payment of $1,018.50, which includes the Contingent Coupon with respect to the fifth Observation Date.&#160;&#160;This payment will be calculated as follows:</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">Principal Amount + Contingent Coupon = $1,000.00 + $18.50 = $1,018.50</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">In this example, the Call Feature limits the term of your investment to approximately fifteen months.&#160;&#160;Further, although each of the Reference Indices has appreciated from the Initial Level on the fifth Observation Date, you only receive a payment of $1,018.50 per Note and do not fully benefit from that appreciation.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block">
<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">
<div style="BORDER-BOTTOM: 0px; TEXT-ALIGN: left; BORDER-LEFT: 0px; PADDING-BOTTOM: 0px; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; PADDING-LEFT: 0px; PADDING-RIGHT: 0px; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; BORDER-TOP: 0px; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; BORDER-RIGHT: 0px; PADDING-TOP: 0px">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">In <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold">Example 3</font>, the closing level of the Worst Performing Reference Index remains below the Coupon Barrier and Trigger Level throughout the term of the Notes.&#160;&#160;As a result, you do not receive any Contingent Coupons during the term of the Notes and, at maturity, you are fully exposed to the decline in this Reference Index.&#160;&#160;As the Final Level of the Worst Performing Reference Index is less than its Trigger Level, the value of the cash that you receive at maturity will be significantly less than the principal amount of the Notes. The payment at maturity will be calculated as follows:</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">Principal Amount + (Principal Amount x Percentage Change of the Worst Performing Reference Index)</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">= $1,000.00 + ($1,000.00 x -40.00%) = $1,000.00 - $400.00 = $600.00</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">In this example, your payment at maturity represents a 40.00% loss, which is proportionate to the decline in the Worst Performing Reference Index.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block">
<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">
<div style="BORDER-BOTTOM: 0px; TEXT-ALIGN: left; BORDER-LEFT: 0px; PADDING-BOTTOM: 0px; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; PADDING-LEFT: 0px; PADDING-RIGHT: 0px; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; BORDER-TOP: 0px; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; BORDER-RIGHT: 0px; PADDING-TOP: 0px">&#160;</div>

<div align="left">
<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">
<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">
<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block"><br>
</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">In <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold">Example 4</font>, the closing level of the Worst Performing Reference Index decreases to a Final Level of $78.&#160;&#160;Although the Final Level of the Worst Performing Reference Index is less than its Initial Level, because the Final Level of the Worst Performing Reference Index is greater than its Trigger Level, you will receive the principal amount plus the Contingent Coupon with respect to the final Observation Date.&#160;&#160;Your payment at maturity would be:</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block"><br>
</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">Principal Amount + Contingent Coupon = $1,000.00 + $18.50 = $1,018.50</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block">
<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">
<div style="BORDER-BOTTOM: 0px; TEXT-ALIGN: left; BORDER-LEFT: 0px; PADDING-BOTTOM: 0px; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; PADDING-LEFT: 0px; PADDING-RIGHT: 0px; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; BORDER-TOP: 0px; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; BORDER-RIGHT: 0px; PADDING-TOP: 0px">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial, sans-serif; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">An investment in the Notes involves significant risks.&#160;&#160;Investing in the Notes is not equivalent to investing directly in either Reference Index.&#160;&#160;These risks are explained in more detail in the section &#8220;Risk Factors,&#8221; beginning on page PS-4 of the product prospectus supplement.&#160;&#160;In addition to the risks described in the prospectus supplement and the product prospectus supplement, you should consider the following:</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div>
<table align="center" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" id="hangingindent" width="100%" style="FONT-FAMILY: arial; FONT-SIZE: 9pt; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: arial">
<tr valign="top">
<td style="WIDTH: 18pt">
<div><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">&#160; </font></div>
</td>
<td style="WIDTH: 18pt">
<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial, sans-serif; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline;" face="Symbol, serif">&#183;</font></font></div>
</td>
<td>
<div align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial, sans-serif; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold">Principal at Risk </font>&#8212; Investors in the Notes could lose some or a substantial portion of their principal amount if there is a decline in the level of the Worst Performing Reference Index between the Pricing Date and the Valuation Date.&#160;&#160;If the Notes are not automatically called and the Final Level of the Worst Performing Reference Index on the Valuation Date is less than the Trigger Level, the amount of cash that you receive at maturity will represent a loss of your principal that is proportionate to the decline in the closing level of the Worst Performing Reference Index through the Valuation Date.&#160;&#160;Any Contingent Coupons received on the Notes prior to the maturity date may not be sufficient to compensate for any such loss.</font></div>
</td>
</tr></table>
</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div>
<table align="center" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" id="hangingindent" width="100%" style="FONT-FAMILY: arial; FONT-SIZE: 9pt; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: arial">
<tr valign="top">
<td style="WIDTH: 18pt">
<div><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">&#160; </font></div>
</td>
<td style="WIDTH: 18pt">
<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial, sans-serif; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline;" face="Symbol, serif">&#183;</font></font></div>
</td>
<td>
<div align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial, sans-serif; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold">The Notes Are Subject to an Automatic Call </font>&#8212; If on any Observation Date on or after September 29, 2015 the closing level of each Reference Index is equal to or greater than its Initial Level, then the Notes will be automatically called. If the Notes are automatically called, then, on the applicable Call Settlement Date, for each $1,000 in principal amount, you will receive $1,000 plus the Contingent Coupon otherwise due on that Call Settlement Date. You will not receive any coupon payments after the Call Settlement Date. You may be unable to reinvest your proceeds from the automatic call in an investment with a return that is as high as the return on the Notes would have been if they had not been called.</font></div>
</td>
</tr></table>
</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div>
<table align="center" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" id="hangingindent" width="100%" style="FONT-FAMILY: arial; FONT-SIZE: 9pt; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: arial">
<tr valign="top">
<td style="WIDTH: 18pt">
<div><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">&#160; </font></div>
</td>
<td style="WIDTH: 18pt">
<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial, sans-serif; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline;" face="Symbol, serif">&#183;</font></font></div>
</td>
<td>
<div align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial, sans-serif; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold">You May Not Receive Any Contingent Coupons </font>&#8212; We will not necessarily make any coupon payments on the Notes.&#160;&#160;If the closing level of either of the Reference Indices on an Observation Date is less than the Coupon Barrier, we will not pay you the Contingent Coupon applicable to that Observation Date. If the closing level of either of the Reference Indices is less than the Coupon Barrier on each of the Observation Dates and on the Valuation Date, we will not pay you any Contingent Coupons during the term of, and you will not receive a positive return on, your Notes. Generally, this non-payment of the Contingent Coupon coincides with a period of greater risk of principal loss on your Notes. Accordingly, if we do not pay the Contingent Coupon on the Maturity Date, you will also incur a loss of principal, because the Final Level of the Worst Performing Reference Index will be less than the Trigger Level.</font></div>
</td>
</tr></table>
</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div>
<table align="center" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" id="hangingindent" width="100%" style="FONT-FAMILY: arial; FONT-SIZE: 9pt; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: arial">
<tr valign="top">
<td style="WIDTH: 18pt">
<div><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">&#160; </font></div>
</td>
<td style="WIDTH: 18pt">
<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial, sans-serif; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline;" face="Symbol, serif">&#183;</font></font></div>
</td>
<td>
<div align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial, sans-serif; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold">Your Payment at Maturity May Be Determined Solely by Reference to the Worst Performing Reference Index Even if the Other Reference Indices Perform Better </font>&#8212; If the Final Level of one of the Reference Indices is less than its applicable Trigger Level, your payment at maturity will be determined by reference to the performance of the Worst Performing Reference Index.&#160;&#160;Even if the Final Levels of the other Reference Indices have increased compared to their Initial Levels, or have experienced a decrease that is less than that of the Worst Performing Reference Index, your return will only be determined by reference to the performance of the Worst Performing Reference Index, regardless of the performance of the other Reference Indices.</font></div>
</td>
</tr></table>
</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div>
<table align="center" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" id="hangingindent" width="100%" style="FONT-FAMILY: arial; FONT-SIZE: 9pt; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: arial">
<tr valign="top">
<td style="WIDTH: 18pt">
<div><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">&#160; </font></div>
</td>
<td style="WIDTH: 18pt">
<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial, sans-serif; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline;" face="Symbol, serif">&#183;</font></font></div>
</td>
<td>
<div align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial, sans-serif; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold">Your Return May Be Lower than the Return on a Conventional Debt Security of Comparable Maturity </font>&#8212; The return that you will receive on the Notes, which could be negative, may be less than the return you could earn on other investments.&#160;&#160;Even if your return is positive, your return may be less than the return you would earn if you bought a conventional senior interest bearing debt security of Royal Bank.</font></div>
</td>
</tr></table>
</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div>
<table align="center" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" id="hangingindent" width="100%" style="FONT-FAMILY: arial; FONT-SIZE: 9pt; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: arial">
<tr valign="top">
<td style="WIDTH: 18pt">
<div><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">&#160; </font></div>
</td>
<td style="WIDTH: 18pt">
<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial, sans-serif; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline;" face="Symbol, serif">&#183;</font></font></div>
</td>
<td>
<div align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial, sans-serif; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold">The Call Feature and the Contingent Coupon Feature Limit Your Potential Return</font> &#8212; The return potential of the Notes is limited to the pre-specified Contingent Coupon Rate, regardless of the appreciation of the Reference Indices. In addition, the total return on the Notes will vary based on the number of Observation Dates on which the Contingent Coupon becomes payable prior to maturity or an automatic call.&#160;&#160;Further, if the Notes are called due to the Call Feature, you will not receive any Contingent Coupons or any other payment in respect of any Observation Dates after the applicable Call Settlement Date. Since the Notes could be called as early as the fourth Observation Date, the total return on the Notes could be minimal. If the Notes are not called, you may be subject to the full downside performance of the Worst Performing Reference Index, even though your potential return is limited to the Contingent Coupon Rate.&#160;&#160;As a result, the return on an investment in the Notes could be less than the return on a direct investment in the Reference Indices.</font></div>
</td>
</tr></table>

</td>
<td>
<div align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial, sans-serif; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold">Payments on the Notes Are Subject to Our Credit Risk, and Changes in Our Credit Ratings Are Expected to Affect the Market Value of the Notes </font>&#8212; The Notes are Royal Bank&#8217;s senior unsecured debt securities.&#160;&#160;As a result, your receipt of the Contingent Coupon payments and the amount due on the maturity date is dependent upon Royal Bank&#8217;s ability to repay its obligations on the applicable payment dates.&#160;&#160;This will be the case even if the levels of the Reference Indices increase after the dates on which their Initial Levels were determined.&#160;&#160;No assurance can be given as to what our financial condition will be at any time during the term of the Notes.</font></div>

</td>
<td>
<div align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial, sans-serif; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold">There May Not Be an Active Trading Market for the Notes&#8212;Sales in the Secondary Market May Result in Significant Losses </font>&#8212; There may be little or no secondary market for the Notes.&#160;&#160;The Notes will not be listed on any securities exchange.&#160;&#160;RBCCM and other affiliates of Royal Bank may make a market for the Notes; however, they are not required to do so.&#160;&#160;RBCCM or any other affiliate of Royal Bank may stop any market-making activities at any time.&#160;&#160;Even if a secondary market for the Notes develops, it may not provide significant liquidity or trade at prices advantageous to you.&#160;&#160;We expect that transaction costs in any secondary market would be high.&#160;&#160;As a result, the difference between bid and asked prices for your Notes in any secondary market could be substantial.</font></div>
</td>
</tr></table>
</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<td>
<div align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial, sans-serif; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold">You Will Not Have Any Rights to the Constituent Stocks Included in either Reference Index </font>&#8212; Investing in the Notes will not make you a holder of any of the constituent stocks of either of the Reference Indices.&#160;&#160;As a holder of the Notes, you will not have voting rights or rights to receive cash dividends or other distributions or other rights that holders of the constituent stocks included in either of the Reference Indices would have.&#160;&#160;The payments on the Notes will not reflect any dividends paid on the securities included in the Reference Indices.</font></div>
</td>
</tr></table>

<div>
<table align="center" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" id="hangingindent" width="100%" style="FONT-FAMILY: arial; FONT-SIZE: 9pt; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: arial">

<td style="WIDTH: 18pt">
<div><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">&#160; </font></div>
</td>
<td style="WIDTH: 18pt">
<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial, sans-serif; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline;" face="Symbol, serif">&#183;</font></font></div>
</td>
<td>
<div align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial, sans-serif; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold">The Initial Estimated Value of the Notes Is Less than the Price to the Public </font>&#8212; The initial estimated value set forth on the cover page of this pricing supplement does not represent a minimum price at which we, RBCCM or any of our affiliates would be willing to purchase the Notes in any secondary market (if any exists) at any time.&#160;&#160;If you attempt to sell the Notes prior to maturity, their market value may be lower than the price you paid for them and the initial estimated value.&#160;&#160;This is due to, among other things, changes in the levels of the Reference Indices, the borrowing rate we pay to issue securities of this kind, and the inclusion in the price to the public of the underwriting discount and the estimated costs relating to our hedging of the Notes.&#160;&#160;These factors, together with various credit, market and economic factors over the term of the Notes, are expected to reduce the price at which you may be able to sell the Notes in any secondary market and will affect the value of the Notes in complex and unpredictable ways.&#160;&#160;Assuming no change in market conditions or any other relevant factors, the price, if any, at which you may be able to sell your Notes prior to maturity may be less than your original purchase price, as any such sale price would not be expected to include the underwriting discount and the hedging costs relating to the Notes. In addition to bid-ask spreads, the value of the Notes determined for any secondary market price is expected to be based on the secondary rate rather than the internal funding rate used to price the Notes and determine the initial estimated value.&#160;&#160;As a result, the secondary price will be less than if the internal funding rate was used.&#160;&#160;The Notes are not designed to be short-term trading instruments.&#160;&#160;Accordingly, you should be able and willing to hold your Notes to maturity.</font></div>
</td>
</tr></table>

<td>
<div align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial, sans-serif; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold">The Initial Estimated Value of the Notes on the Cover Page Is an Estimate Only, Calculated as of the Time the Terms of the Notes Are Set </font>&#8212; The initial estimated value of the Notes is based on the value of our obligation to make the payments on the Notes, together with the mid-market value of the derivative embedded in the terms of the Notes.&#160;&#160;See &#8220;Structuring the Notes&#8221; below.&#160;&#160;Our estimate is based on a variety of assumptions, including our credit spreads, expectations as to dividends, interest rates and volatility, and the expected term of the Notes.&#160;&#160;These assumptions are based on certain forecasts about future events, which may prove to be incorrect.&#160;&#160;Other entities may value the Notes or similar securities at a price that is significantly different than we do.</font></div>
</td>
</tr></table>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial, sans-serif; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">The value of the Notes at any time after the Pricing Date will vary based on many factors, including changes in market conditions, and cannot be predicted with accuracy.&#160;&#160;As a result, the actual value you would receive if you sold the Notes in any secondary market, if any, should be expected to differ materially from the initial estimated value of your Notes.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial, sans-serif; COLOR: #17365d; FONT-SIZE: 14pt; FONT-WEIGHT: bold">INFORMATION REGARDING THE REFERENCE INDICES</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">All disclosures contained in this pricing supplement regarding the Reference Indices, including, without limitation, their make-up, method of calculation, and changes in their components, have been derived from publicly available sources. The information reflects the policies of, and is subject to change by, the applicable index sponsor.&#160;&#160;Each of these sponsors has no obligation to continue to publish, and may discontinue publication of, the applicable Reference Index. The consequences of an index sponsor discontinuing publication of a Reference Index are discussed in the section of the product prospectus supplement entitled &#8220;General Terms of the Notes&#8212;Unavailability of the Level of a Reference Index.&#8221; Neither we nor RBCCM accepts any responsibility for the calculation, maintenance or publication of either Reference Index or any successor index.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-WEIGHT: bold">The SPX</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">The SPX is intended to provide an indication of the pattern of common stock price movement. The calculation of the level of the SPX is based on the relative value of the aggregate market value of the common stocks of 500 companies as of a particular time compared to the aggregate average market value of the common stocks of 500 similar companies during the base period of the years 1941 through 1943. As of August 29, 2014, 389 companies included in the SPX traded on the New York Stock Exchange, and 111 companies included in the SPX traded on The NASDAQ Stock Market. On August 29, 2014, the average market capitalization of the companies included in the SPX was $37.57 billion. As of that date, the largest component of the SPX had a market capitalization of $618.05 billion, and the smallest component of the SPX had a market capitalization of $4.11 billion.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">S&amp;P Dow Jones Indices LLC chooses companies for inclusion in the SPX with the aim of achieving a distribution by broad industry groupings that approximates the distribution of these groupings in the common stock population of its Stock Guide Database of over 10,000 companies, which S&amp;P Dow Jones Indices LLC uses as an assumed model for the composition of the total market. Relevant criteria employed by S&amp;P Dow Jones Indices LLC include the viability of the particular company, the extent to which that company represents the industry group to which it is assigned, the extent to which the market price of that company&#8217;s common stock generally is responsive to changes in the affairs of the respective industry, and the market value and trading activity of the common stock of that company. Ten main groups of companies comprise the SPX, with the approximate percentage of the market capitalization of the SPX included in each group as of August 29, 2014, indicated in parentheses: Consumer Discretionary (11.9%); Consumer Staples (9.4%); Energy (10.4%); Financials (16.1%); Health Care (13.7%); Industrials (10.2%); Information Technology (19.4%); Materials (3.5%); Telecommunication Services (2.4%); and Utilities (3.0%). S&amp;P from time to time, in its sole discretion, may add companies to, or delete companies from, the SPX to achieve the objectives stated above.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">S&amp;P Dow Jones Indices LLC calculates the SPX by reference to the prices of the constituent stocks of the SPX without taking account of the value of dividends paid on those stocks. As a result, the return on the Notes will not reflect the return you would realize if you actually owned the SPX constituent stocks and received the dividends paid on those stocks.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-WEIGHT: bold">Computation of the SPX</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">While S&amp;P Dow Jones Indices LLC currently employs the following methodology to calculate the SPX, no assurance can be given that S&amp;P Dow Jones Indices LLC will not modify or change this methodology in a manner that may affect the Payment at Maturity.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">Historically, the market value of any component stock of the SPX was calculated as the product of the market price per share and the number of then outstanding shares of such component stock. In March 2005, S&amp;P Dow Jones Indices LLC began shifting the SPX halfway from a market capitalization weighted formula to a float-adjusted formula, before moving the SPX to full float adjustment on September 16, 2005. S&amp;P Dow Jones Indices LLC&#8217;s criteria for selecting stocks for the SPX did not change with the shift to float adjustment. However, the adjustment affects each company&#8217;s weight in the SPX.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">Under float adjustment, the share counts used in calculating the SPX reflect only those shares that are available to investors, not all of a company&#8217;s outstanding shares. Float adjustment excludes shares that are closely held by control groups, other publicly traded companies or government agencies.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">
<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">
<div style="BORDER-BOTTOM: 0px; TEXT-ALIGN: left; BORDER-LEFT: 0px; PADDING-BOTTOM: 0px; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; PADDING-LEFT: 0px; PADDING-RIGHT: 0px; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; BORDER-TOP: 0px; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; BORDER-RIGHT: 0px; PADDING-TOP: 0px">&#160;</div>

<div align="left">
<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">
<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">
<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: arial; COLOR: #17365d; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">Trigger Phoenix Autocallable Yield Notes</font></font></font></font></font></font></font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: arial; COLOR: #17365d; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">Two Equity Indices, due October 4, 2017</font></font></font></font></font></font></font></div>

</div>
</td>
</tr><tr bgcolor="#b7c3d9">
<td valign="top" width="30%">
<div>&#160;</div>

<div>&#160;</div>
</td>
<td valign="top" width="40%"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">&#160;</font></td>
<td align="left" valign="top" width="30%">
<div><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">&#160; </font></div>

<div><font color="#17365d" size="2" style="FONT-FAMILY: arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">&#160;&#160; </font></div>
</td>
</tr></table>
</div>
</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block">&#160;</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">In September 2012, all shareholdings representing more than 5% of a stock&#8217;s outstanding shares, other than holdings by &#8220;block owners,&#8221; were removed from the float for purposes of calculating the SPX.&#160;&#160;Generally, these &#8220;control holders&#8221; will include officers and directors, private equity, venture capital and special equity firms, other publicly traded companies that hold shares for control, strategic partners, holders of restricted shares, ESOPs, employee and family trusts, foundations associated with the company, holders of unlisted share classes of stock, government entities at all levels (other than government retirement/pension funds) and any individual person who controls a 5% or greater stake in a company as reported in regulatory filings.&#160;&#160;However, holdings by block owners, such as depositary banks, pension funds, mutual funds and ETF providers, 401(k) plans of the company, government retirement/pension funds, investment funds of insurance companies, asset managers and investment funds, independent foundations and savings and investment plans, will ordinarily be considered part of the float.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">Treasury stock, stock options, restricted shares, equity participation units, warrants, preferred stock, convertible stock, and rights are not part of the float. Shares held in a trust to allow investors in countries outside the country of domicile, such as depositary shares and Canadian exchangeable shares are normally part of the float unless those shares form a control block.&#160;&#160;If a company has multiple classes of stock outstanding, shares in an unlisted or non-traded class are treated as a control block.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">For each stock, an investable weight factor (&#8220;IWF&#8221;) is calculated by dividing the available float shares by the total shares outstanding.&#160;&#160;As of September 21, 2012, available float shares are defined as the total shares outstanding less shares held by control holders.&#160;&#160;This calculation is subject to a 5% minimum threshold for control blocks.&#160;&#160;For example, if a company&#8217;s officers and directors hold 3% of the company&#8217;s shares, and no other control group holds 5% of the company&#8217;s shares, S&amp;P Dow Jones Indices LLC would assign that company an IWF of 1.00, as no control group meets the 5% threshold.&#160;&#160;However, if a company&#8217;s officers and directors hold 3% of the company&#8217;s shares and another control group holds 20% of the company&#8217;s shares, S&amp;P Dow Jones Indices LLC would assign an IWF of 0.77, reflecting the fact that 23% of the company&#8217;s outstanding shares are considered to be held for control.&#160;&#160;For companies with multiple classes of stock, S&amp;P Dow Jones Indices LLC calculates the weighted average IWF for each stock using the proportion of the total company market capitalization of each share class as weights.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">The SPX is calculated using a base-weighted aggregate methodology. The level of the SPX reflects the total market value of all 500 component stocks relative to the base period of the years 1941 through 1943. An indexed number is used to represent the results of this calculation in order to make the level easier to use and track over time. The actual total market value of the component stocks during the base period of the years 1941 through 1943 has been set to an indexed level of 10. This is often indicated by the notation 1941-43 = 10. In practice, the daily calculation of the SPX is computed by dividing the total market value of the component stocks by the &#8220;index divisor.&#8221; By itself, the index divisor is an arbitrary number. However, in the context of the calculation of the SPX, it serves as a link to the original base period level of the SPX. The index divisor keeps the SPX comparable over time and is the manipulation point for all adjustments to the SPX, which is index maintenance.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-WEIGHT: bold">Index Maintenance</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">Index maintenance includes monitoring and completing the adjustments for company additions and deletions, share changes, stock splits, stock dividends, and stock price adjustments due to company restructuring or spinoffs. Some corporate actions, such as stock splits and stock dividends, require changes in the common shares outstanding and the stock prices of the companies in the SPX, and do not require index divisor adjustments.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">To prevent the level of the SPX from changing due to corporate actions, corporate actions which affect the total market value of the SPX require an index divisor adjustment. By adjusting the index divisor for the change in market value, the level of the SPX remains constant and does not reflect the corporate actions of individual companies in the SPX. Index divisor adjustments are made after the close of trading and after the calculation of the SPX closing level.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">
<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">
<div style="BORDER-BOTTOM: 0px; TEXT-ALIGN: left; BORDER-LEFT: 0px; PADDING-BOTTOM: 0px; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; PADDING-LEFT: 0px; PADDING-RIGHT: 0px; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; BORDER-TOP: 0px; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; BORDER-RIGHT: 0px; PADDING-TOP: 0px">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">Changes in a company&#8217;s shares outstanding of 5.00% or more due to mergers, acquisitions, public offerings, tender offers, Dutch auctions, or exchange offers are made as soon as reasonably possible. All other changes of 5.00% or more (due to, for example, company stock repurchases, private placements, redemptions, exercise of options, warrants, conversion of preferred stock, notes, debt, equity participation units, at the market offerings, or other recapitalizations) are made weekly and are announced on Wednesdays for implementation after the close of trading on the following Wednesday. Changes of less than 5.00% due to a company&#8217;s acquisition of another company in the SPX are made as soon as reasonably possible. All other changes of less than 5.00% are accumulated and made quarterly on the third Friday of March, June, September, and December, and are usually announced two to five days prior.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">Changes in IWFs of more than five percentage points caused by corporate actions (such as merger and acquisition activity, restructurings, or spinoffs) will be made as soon as reasonably possible. Other changes in IWFs will be made annually when IWFs are reviewed.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-WEIGHT: bold">The SX5E</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">The SX5E was created by STOXX Limited (&#8220;STOXX&#8221;), as a joint venture between Deutsche B&#246;rse AG and SIX Group AG.&#160;&#160;Publication of the Index began in February 1998, based on an initial level of 1,000 at December 31, 1991.&#160;&#160;Changes to the component stocks are implemented on the third Friday in September and are effective the following trading day.&#160;&#160;Changes in the composition of the SX5E are made to ensure that the Index includes the 50 market sector leaders from within the Dow Jones EURO STOXX Total Market Index.&#160;&#160;Additional information about the Index is available on the STOXX website: <font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">http://www.stoxx.com</font>.&#160;&#160;However, information included in that website is not included or incorporated by reference in this pricing supplement.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">For each of the 19 EURO STOXX regional supersector indices, the stocks are ranked in terms of free-float market capitalization.&#160;&#160;The largest stocks are added to the selection list until the coverage is close to, but still less than, 60% of the free-float market capitalization of the corresponding supersector index.&#160;&#160;If the next highest-ranked stock brings the coverage closer to 60% in absolute terms, then it is also added to the selection list. All current stocks in the SX5E are then added to the selection list.&#160;&#160;All of the stocks on the selection list are then ranked in terms of free-float market capitalization to produce the final index selection list.&#160;&#160;The largest 40 stocks on the selection list are selected; the remaining 10 stocks are selected from the largest remaining current stocks ranked between 41 and 60; if the number of stocks selected is still below 50, then the largest remaining stocks are selected until there are 50 stocks. In exceptional cases, STOXX&#8217;s management board can add stocks to and remove them from the selection list.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">The index components are subject to a capped maximum index weight of 10%, which is applied on a quarterly basis.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">The SX5E is composed of 50 component stocks of market sector leaders from within the EURO STOXX<font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 70%; VERTICAL-ALIGN: text-top">&#174;</font> supersector indices, which includes stocks selected from the Eurozone portion of the STOXX Europe 600<font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 70%; VERTICAL-ALIGN: text-top">&#174; </font>supersector indices. The component stocks have a high degree of liquidity and represent the largest companies across a wide range of market sectors.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-WEIGHT: bold">Index Composition and Maintenance</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">The composition of the SX5E is reviewed annually, based on the closing stock data on the last trading day in August.&#160;&#160;The component stocks are announced on the first trading day in September.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">The free float factors for each component stock used to calculate the<font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 12pt">&#160;</font>SX5E, as described below, are reviewed, calculated, and implemented on a quarterly basis and are fixed until the next quarterly review.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">The SX5E is subject to a &#8220;fast exit rule.&#8221;&#160;&#160;The index components are monitored for any changes based on the monthly selection list ranking.&#160;&#160;A stock is deleted from the SX5E if: (a) it ranks 75 or below on the monthly selection list and (b) it has been ranked 75 or below for a consecutive period of two months in the monthly selection list.&#160;&#160;The highest-ranked stock that is not an index component will replace it.&#160;&#160;Changes will be implemented on the close of the fifth trading day of the month, and are effective the next trading day.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">The SX5E is also subject to a &#8220;fast entry rule.&#8221;&#160;&#160;All stocks on the latest selection lists and initial public offering (IPO) stocks are reviewed for a fast-track addition on a quarterly basis. A stock is added, if (a) it qualifies for the latest STOXX blue-chip selection list generated end of February, May, August or November and (b) it ranks within the &#8220;lower buffer&#8221; on this selection list.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">The SX5E is also reviewed on an ongoing basis.&#160;&#160;Corporate actions (including initial public offerings, mergers and takeovers, spin-offs, delistings, and bankruptcy) that affect the index composition are immediately reviewed.&#160;&#160;Any changes are announced, implemented, and effective in line with the type of corporate action and the magnitude of the effect.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-WEIGHT: bold">Index Calculation</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">The SX5E is calculated with the &#8220;Laspeyres formula,&#8221; which measures the aggregate price changes in the component stocks against a fixed base quantity weight.&#160;&#160;The formula for calculating the index value can be expressed as follows:</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">Index = <font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">free float market capitalization of the Index at the time&#160;&#160;</font>&#160;&#160;x 1000</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">adjusted base date market capitalization of the Index</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">
<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">
<div style="BORDER-BOTTOM: 0px; TEXT-ALIGN: left; BORDER-LEFT: 0px; PADDING-BOTTOM: 0px; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; PADDING-LEFT: 0px; PADDING-RIGHT: 0px; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; BORDER-TOP: 0px; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; BORDER-RIGHT: 0px; PADDING-TOP: 0px">&#160;</div>

<div align="left">
<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">
<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">
<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">
<div align="left">
<div id="PGBRK" style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt">
<div id="FTR">
<div id="GLFTR" style="TEXT-ALIGN: right; WIDTH: 100%">
<div style="TEXT-ALIGN: right; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt">
<div style="TEXT-ALIGN: right; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">RBC Capital Markets, LLC</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">The &#8220;free float market capitalization of the Index&#8221; is equal to the sum of the products of the closing price, market capitalization and free float factor, as of the time that the SX5E is being calculated. The divisor of the SX5E is adjusted to maintain the continuity of the SX5E&#8217;s values across changes due to corporate actions, such as the deletion and addition of stocks, the substitution of stocks, stock dividends, and stock splits.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: arial; COLOR: #17365d; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">Linked to the Worst Performing of</font></font></font></font></font></font></font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: arial; COLOR: #17365d; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">Two Equity Indices, due October 4, 2017</font></font></font></font></font></font></font></div>

</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial, sans-serif; COLOR: #17365d; FONT-SIZE: 14pt; FONT-WEIGHT: bold">SUPPLEMENTAL PLAN OF DISTRIBUTION (CONFLICTS OF INTEREST)</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">Delivery of the Notes will be made against payment for the Notes on October 2, 2014, which is the third (3rd) business day following the Pricing Date (this settlement cycle being referred to as &#8220;T+3&#8221;).&#160;&#160;See &#8220;Plan of Distribution&#8221; in the prospectus dated July 23, 2013. For additional information as to the relationship between us and RBCCM, please see the section &#8220;Plan of Distribution&#8212;Conflicts of Interest&#8221; in the prospectus dated July 23, 2013.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">The value of the Notes shown on your account statement may be based on RBCCM&#8217;s estimate of the value of the Notes if RBCCM or another of our affiliates were to make a market in the Notes (which it is not obligated to do).&#160;&#160;That estimate will be based upon the price that RBCCM may pay for the Notes in light of then-prevailing market conditions, our creditworthiness and transaction costs.&#160;&#160;For a period of approximately three months after the issue date of the Notes, the value of the Notes that may be shown on your account statement may be higher than RBCCM&#8217;s estimated value of the Notes at that time.&#160;&#160;This is because the estimated value of the Notes will not include the underwriting discount and our hedging costs and profits; however, the value of the Notes shown on your account statement during that period is initially expected to be a higher amount, reflecting the addition of RBCCM&#8217;s underwriting discount and our estimated costs and profits from hedging the Notes.&#160;&#160;This excess is expected to decrease over time until the end of this period.&#160;&#160;After this period, if RBCCM repurchases your Notes, it expects to do so at prices that reflect their estimated value.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial, sans-serif; COLOR: #17365d; FONT-SIZE: 14pt; FONT-WEIGHT: bold">STRUCTURING THE NOTES</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">The Notes are our debt securities, the return on which is linked to the performance of each of the Reference Indices.&#160;&#160;As is the case for all of our debt securities, including our structured notes, the economic terms of the Notes reflect our actual or perceived creditworthiness at the time of pricing.&#160;&#160;In addition, because structured notes result in increased operational, funding and liability management costs to us, we typically borrow the funds under these Notes at a rate that is more favorable to us than the rate that we might pay for a conventional fixed or floating rate debt security of comparable maturity.&#160;&#160;Using this relatively lower implied borrowing rate rather than the secondary market rate, is a factor that reduced the initial estimated value of the Notes at the time their terms were set. Unlike the estimated value included in this pricing supplement, any value of the Notes determined for purposes of a secondary market transaction may be based on a different funding rate, which may result in a lower value for the Notes than if our initial internal funding rate were used.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">In order to satisfy our payment obligations under the Notes, we may choose to enter into certain hedging arrangements (which may include call options, put options or other derivatives) on the issue date with RBCCM or one of our other subsidiaries.&#160;&#160;The terms of these hedging arrangements take into account a number of factors, including our creditworthiness, interest rate movements, the volatility of the Reference Indices, and the tenor of the Notes.&#160;&#160;The economic terms of the Notes and their initial estimated value depend in part on the terms of these hedging arrangements.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">The lower implied borrowing rate is a factor that reduced the economic terms of the Notes to you.&#160;&#160;The initial offering price of the Notes also reflects the underwriting commission and our estimated hedging costs.&#160;&#160;These factors resulted in the initial estimated value for the Notes on the Pricing Date being less than their public offering price.&#160;&#160;See &#8220;Selected Risk Factors&#8212;The Initial Estimated Value of the Notes Is Less than the Price to the Public&#8221; above.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">
<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">
<div style="BORDER-BOTTOM: 0px; TEXT-ALIGN: left; BORDER-LEFT: 0px; PADDING-BOTTOM: 0px; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; PADDING-LEFT: 0px; PADDING-RIGHT: 0px; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; BORDER-TOP: 0px; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; BORDER-RIGHT: 0px; PADDING-TOP: 0px">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial, sans-serif; COLOR: #17365d; FONT-SIZE: 14pt; FONT-WEIGHT: bold">SUPPLEMENTAL DISCUSSION OF U.S. FEDERAL INCOME TAX CONSEQUENCES</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">&#160;</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">The following disclosure supplements, and to the extent inconsistent, supersedes, the discussion in the product prospectus supplement dated July 25, 2013 under &#8220;Supplemental Discussion of U.S. Federal Income Tax Consequences.&#8221;</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">A &#8220;dividend equivalent&#8221; payment is treated as a dividend from sources within the U.S. and such payments generally would be subject to a 30% U.S. withholding tax if paid to a non-U.S. holder.&#160;&#160;Under proposed Treasury Department regulations, certain payments (including deemed payments) that are contingent upon or determined by reference to actual or estimated U.S. source dividends, with respect to certain equity-linked instruments, whether explicitly stated or implicitly taken into account in computing one or more of the terms of such instruments, including the securities, may be treated as dividend equivalents.&#160;&#160;If enacted in their current form, the regulations will impose a withholding tax on payments or deemed payments made on the securities on or after January 1, 2016 that are treated as dividend equivalents.&#160;&#160;However, the U.S. Treasury Department and Internal Revenue Service have announced that they intend to limit this withholding to equity-linked instruments issued on or after the date that is 90 days after the date of publication in the U.S. Federal Register of final regulations addressing dividend equivalent withholding. If any payments are treated as dividend equivalents subject to withholding, we (or the applicable paying agent) would be entitled to withhold taxes without being required to pay any additional amounts with respect to amounts so withheld.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial, sans-serif; COLOR: #17365d; FONT-SIZE: 14pt; FONT-WEIGHT: bold">VALIDITY OF THE NOTES</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">In the opinion of Norton Rose Fulbright Canada LLP, the issue and sale of the Notes has been duly authorized by all necessary corporate action of the Bank in conformity with the Indenture, and when the Notes have been duly executed, authenticated and issued in accordance with the Indenture, the Notes will be validly issued and, to the extent validity of the Notes is a matter governed by the laws of the Province of Ontario or Qu&#233;bec, or the laws of Canada applicable therein, and will be valid obligations of the Bank, subject to applicable bankruptcy, insolvency and other laws of general application affecting creditors&#8217; rights, equitable principles, and subject to limitations as to the currency in which judgments in Canada may be rendered, as prescribed by the Currency Act (Canada).&#160;&#160;This opinion is given as of the date hereof and is limited to the laws of the Provinces of Ontario and Quebec and the federal laws of Canada applicable thereto.&#160;&#160;In addition, this opinion is subject to customary assumptions about the Trustee&#8217;s authorization, execution and delivery of the Indenture and the genuineness of signatures and certain factual matters, all as stated in the letter of such counsel dated July 24, 2013, which has been filed as Exhibit 5.1 to Royal Bank&#8217;s Form 6-K filed with the SEC on July 24, 2013.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Arial; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">In the opinion of Morrison &amp; Foerster LLP, when the Notes have been duly completed in accordance with the Indenture and issued and sold as contemplated by the prospectus supplement and the prospectus, the Notes will be valid, binding and enforceable obligations of Royal Bank, entitled to the benefits of the Indenture, subject to applicable bankruptcy, insolvency and similar laws affecting creditors&#8217; rights generally, concepts of reasonableness and equitable principles of general applicability (including, without limitation, concepts of good faith, fair dealing and the lack of bad faith).&#160;&#160;This opinion is given as of the date hereof and is limited to the laws of the State of New York.&#160;&#160;This opinion is subject to customary assumptions about the Trustee&#8217;s authorization, execution and delivery of the Indenture and the genuineness of signatures and to such counsel&#8217;s reliance on the Bank and other sources as to certain factual matters, all as stated in the legal opinion dated July 24, 2013, which has been filed as Exhibit 5.2 to the Bank&#8217;s Form 6-K dated July 24, 2013.</font></div>

<div style="TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
